<Author>garethellis36
<Content>Magnifique My fianc茅e and I stayed 3 nights at the Royal Magda Etoile this past weekend, and it was one of the best hotel experiences we have ever had - possible *the* best.Upon arrival into the beautifully appointed lobby area, we were greeted by a charming and friendly receptionist. This theme continued throughout our stay, and the male receptionist who was on late at night was especially helpful - he helped us find a restaurant and then checked us in for our flight home on his computer. What service!Our room was small and cosy, but we were not in Paris to sit around in a hotel anyway, so it was ideal. The decor was modern, the room clean and the bed comfortable. The bathroom was a decent size, and was also very clean. The shower was worth particulate mention, as it was very powerful and the water was very hot.Breakfast was expensive at 鈧?2 for a simple buffet, so we didn't sample that - there are plenty of cafes and other places to get a bite nearby. The location in general is excellent, being just a short walk from the Charles de Gaulle-Etoile Metro  RER station, which is under the Arc de Triomphe. The hotel is down a quiet side street off Ave de Wagram, so there is little road noise and what little noise there is outside is kept out by the double-glazed windows.One local tip we would give is to try the bistro Le Hide (www.lehide.fr) just around the corner on Rue du General Lanrezac. We had 2 courses each and 50cl of vin blanc for 鈧?6, and it was one of the best meals we've had. Like the hotel, the bistro is something of a hidden gem.In summary, we would not hesitate to recommend this charming little hotel to anyone who is looking for a good base for a break in Paris. We are very happy customers!

<Author>WanderingClown
<Content>Great location, lovely hotel, welcoming staff Booking a hotel in Paris for me, my daughter (8), my Father and his son (11) was almost overwhelming - we could have stayed at something more expensive but might have missed the charm of Paris. What we were looking for was something reasonably priced, but as we were only there from Friday to Monday was ideally located for the sights, open top tour bus stop, easy eats, and offered a straightforward way of getting to Disneyland Paris and Gare du Nord. This hotel ticked all the boxes. Just a hundred or so yards from an exit of Charles de Gaulles Etoile station this provided us with a minimum of fuss at the start and end of our days. (Buy a Paris Visite ticket before you go to give you full access to central Paris transport). Booking directly with the hotel via e-mail was so easy - immediate replies to questions and to the booking. When we arrived it was obvious why - there was always a member of staff around the reception desk ready to say hello or to wish you a nice day, or to answer any questions you might have. One thing stuck in my mind - a small thing perhaps, but underlined the care that the staff of this small hotel takes. All tables were busy for breakfast one morning, so we waited around the corner in the reception area. Every couple of minutes the receptionist popped round to check if a table had become free, until shortly they showed us to a free table. This attention really makes a difference - we felt welcome throughout our stay.The hotel is situated near the Champs Elysees and a couple of hundred yards away from the Arc de Triomphe. Walk 50 yards up the street and you can see the Arc and the Eiffel Tower sits in the distance. Open top bus tours (we went for L'Open Tour and weren't disappointed) stop within a few hundred yards. Disneyland Paris is 45 minutes away on the RER that runs directly from Charles de Gaulle Etoile station, so catch that 1 hour before park opening and you'll be knocking on the door of the park at just the right time. Be aware that you will need to ensure you have tickets for the right zones to get to Disney. We bought 1-3 Paris Visite tickets and separate tickets to get to Disney. (We used www.allofrance.co.uk for our tickets so that we didn't waste time when we got there).The rooms we stayed in were small but clean. I was particularly pleased with the bathroom. During our stay I didn't once find anything I could fault regarding the cleanliness. Breakfast, as already mentioned, was simple and at 鈧?2 a little expensive but spend a little time over your muesli and yoghurt, croissants, bread, cheese and meats, fruit and coffees while deciding on your plan for the day and it was wholly worthwhile. Across the side street was a sandwich shop that made sandwiches and salads to order, and McDonalds was 50 yards away from the hotel - one night we took it back to our room as we didn't have the energy to dine out. The Italian restaurant at the end of the road and across the street was very good, and because of the location there were many other eateries to choose from.All in all, I left with the satisfaction that I had managed to pick out a winning hotel from the many, many hotels on offer in Paris. Suffice to say that a similar trip in years to come will be much easier as I'll simply book again! And if friends want to visit Paris, I'll be confident in recommending this little gem.  
<Date>Nov 16, 2008

<Author>theneills
<Content>Wee gem! We've been to Paris several times and this hotel is a real discovery. It's in a perfect position, 3 minutes from the Arc de Triomphe, Metro/RER (Etoile) and the express bus from Charles de Gaulle Airport. It's also only a short walk from the Porte de Maillot where the bus from Beauvais Airport (Ryanair Wizz etc) gets in to Paris. The hotel is beautifully decorated, absolutely spotless and very quiet (open the windows to appreciate how good they are at sound-deadening). The price is extremely reasonable for the position: it isn't cheap compared to some hotels but the latter will be out of the centre and perhaps in what might appear to be an unsafe area. All things considered, the Magda Etoile is a real bargain. But we've left the best until last: the staff are wonderfully friendly and helpful. We had no problems with anything therefore had relatively few dealings with them, but they were always extremely friendly and welcoming. Breakfast isn't included in the room price but serves the best cup of tea in Paris (and believe us we've had some horrors in other hotels). Criticisms? The lift is small and the rooms are smaller than USA size, but you need to remember that you're in a renovated old building in the centre of Paris so rooms can't be enormous if they are to have an en-suite. They are perfectly adequate and the beds are large and comfortable. The wall-mounted flat-screen TV is good as well.

<Author>Peg70
<Content>Paris's Single Greatest Attraction! An absolute delight! We were in Paris for a week with our three teenaged children at the end of a three-week European trip. This small boutique hotel manages to offer all the important services and amenities of its much better-known and much more expensive competition. The rooms are clean, well-appointed with mini-bars, room safes, bathroom goodies and comfortable beds. This hotel really outdoes itself when it comes to its front-desk staff. Each of the five desk staff we met were unfailingly cheerful, polite, enormously helpful and attentive. One truly gets the impression they enjoy what they do and take great pride in making each and every guest as happy and comfortable as possible: A rare attitude these days, even at four times the price of this exceptional little find. A special mention must be made of Yohan. Pulling 12 hr. day shifts on the front desk, he saved our holiday from certain disaster as we had misplaced/left behind critical medication for one of our children. Because it is a drug that is very tightly controlled in Italy and France, we were told that it was entirely impossible to procure (even with a faxed prescription from our Canadian doctor). As we were considering a very early end to our holiday, Yohan took it upon himself to spend 3 hrs. one afternoon turning the citys' medical community inside out. The result was the impossible: Yohan had arranged for a psychiatrist to visit us at the hotel and write a French prescription for our daughter. Additionally, when the evening desk manager arrived, we found he had been fully briefed on our situation and was awaiting the psychiatrist's arrival. Find me a Four Season's staff or anyone at the George V who would go that far above and beyond and I'll pay for your next stay! This lovely, accommodating, ideally located, quiet and pretty hotel has this family's undying loyalty and admiration. You simply cannot go wrong.

(I normally don鈥檛 mind if the desk people are super friendly or not, but in a foreign country it always feels good to have someone greet you warmly in any language.) The hotel was old-fashioned, but extremely well maintained with modern necessities. Every need we had was met. Something important to me, which was a nice surprise, was the fact that the bedroom had a door separating it from the front room (which had a comfy fold out queen bed). I was able to relax and watch CNN while my teenagers relaxed and watched what they wanted in their room as we unwound after a day of sight-seeing. The bathroom was also extremely upgraded and large. The breakfast was typical continental fare (yummy variety of cheeses and baguettes), which they gave the option to have as room service if we wanted. I would stay here because of the hotel alone, but the customer service was a bonus, and it helped to make our stay even more memorable.

<Author>Supratik
<Content>Excellent value for money I always pay more attention to comments from fellow travellers rather than the guide books and I am glad to say that this time also I did not regret my decision. Direct booking was easy, e-mails answered promptly. Stayed in room 311, an apartment suite with two adjoining rooms (one with a sofabed) with plenty of room for my daughters (8  3 years) to jump around. Separate TV for them as well !! Rooms smallish by North American standard but excellent by Paris standard !! Furnishing simple but adequate. Bed very comfortable. Nice spacious bathroom with good water pressure. No tea/coffee in room but they provided us with a kettle. Minibar expensive as usual. We kept milk in the fridge for our children and no one objected.Location is superb. It took us 20 minutes and 13 euros by taxi from Gare-du-Nord, travelling on a Saturday afternoon. CDG Etoile is 5 minutes walk. 47 minutes to Disneyland by RER. Jardin d'Acclimatation was just 20 minutes walk and we had much more fun there compared to the sugar coated commercialism of Disneyland. Strongly recommended if you have young children.Breakfast slightly pricey and we ate for first two days only. Plenty of eateries within easy reach including McDonald, Quick and Hippopotamus . There is a branch of Monoprix supermarket very close for grocery and other stuff. All the staff were very friendly with special thanks to Aurelle and Yohann.My only gripe is that soundproofing is less than satisfactory and on the first night my sleep was badly affected by 2 little girls running in the corridoor between 2 rooms. This restarted again next night around midnight and this time I had to speak to their guardians politely but firmly and thankfully it stopped. The familes moved away subsequently and I had reasonably peaceful nights afterwards although we could hear our upstairs neighbours from time to time. On the whole a very satisfying experience and I won't hesitate to recommend this hotel for families.

<Author>td1208
<Content>Excellent location. Enjoyed our stay at Royal Magda Etoile Hotel. My wife and I chose this hotel for our Paris vacation, based on tripadvisor reviews. We were very pleased with our 6-night stay at Royal Magda Etoile Hotel during the last week of June.Sidebar: We took the Air France bus shuttle from Charles de Gaulle Airport to Arc de Triomphe. Extremely rough baggage handling by Air France shuttle bus staff, resulted in the zipper of our suitcase being badly damaged, despite the suitcase being in perfect condition after overnight travel from Toronto, Canada, to Paris, with stopovers in Montreal, Munich and Rome, on various airlines. This damage rendered the suitcase not being able to be properly closed, as the slider was completely removed from the teeth of zipper. While this may not seem like the end of the world to readers, this was not a good start to our trip, given that we were traveling elsewhere in Europe, the week following.The hotel is a very short walk from Air France bus shuttle stop. We were greeted at reception desk by Yohan, who was very helpful. Upon learning about our misfortune, he summoned help to repair the zipper on our suitcase. Sassy (hotel maintenance) immediately repaired the zipper, in the area right beside the lobby. One would never have known that it was ever broken. When offered a small token of our appreciation, Sassy very graciously declined, saying it was his pleasure to help. The hotel鈥檚 owner, Mr. Destouches, happened to be in the lobby at the time, so we made sure that Sassy鈥檚 service was duly recognized. Upon our insistence, Sassy very reluctantly accepted our envelope. As well, I had brought my laptop on our trip. Without hesitation, Yohan offered to lend an Internet cable and voltage converter for our entire stay. From the time of our arrival at the hotel, to after check-in, the staff at this hotel, turned our unfortunate start (though not related to the hotel whatsoever), into a positive. For this, we were thankful. Other staff (Juliet, head housekeeper) was helpful. Soukri, at reception in evening, always welcomed us with a warm smile and conversation at the end of our busy day.The location of this hotel is ideal. Everything is within a very short walking distance - Metro station, from which one can travel virtually everywhere in Paris; Arc de Triomphe; restaurants; caf茅s; retail, convenience and grocery stores; and coin laundry (thanks for the local map and directions, Yohan).Our room was small (which we knew beforehand from reading reviews), but a great value. It was tastefully decorated and modern, in very good condition, very clean, and air conditioning worked. Our bed was comfortable. The desk allowed for use of our laptop, and free in-room Internet connection worked perfectly. We bought an international phone card externally, and used the in room phone, which worked well to make calls to Canada. We made good use of in-room safe, as well.Overall, we would recommend this hotel to those traveling to Paris.

<Author>travelerLondonON
<Content>Just as we expected Our family of 6 (2 grandparents, 2 adults, 2 children) stayed here in early July for 5 nights. We had 2 rooms. One was a club room for 2, and the second room was a Suite for 4, which had a separate bedroom and a livingroom with a pull out sofa. The suite had less streat noise. I believe that all the suites face the rear courtyard which is quiter.The hotel and rooms were very clean and nicely renovated. The bathrooms were very nice. There is a small elevator to bring up the suitcases when checking in or checking out. Otherwise we used the stairs. As is common to most Paris hotels in this category, the walls are thin. We expected this and came prepared with earplugs. Without earplugs, we were able to hear people talking in other rooms and doors opening and closing in the hallways late into the night. With earplugs it was no problem at all. We definitely recommend bringing earplugs.The front desk staff were all very helpful and pleasant. They all spoke excellent english, and did not seem to mind speaking english instead of french. Lily was especially nice to us, and made us feel very welcome. She gave us good information regarding which restaurants in the area were good with children, and the location of grocery stores. She provided us with a kettle, cups, plates, and some utensils, so we were able to make instant coffee and tea in the rooms, and prepare snacks for the kids. They allowed us to use the fridge to hold our own drinks and food, rather than using it as a minibar. This made the hotel much more functional for us. We were able to bring in breakfast and save a lot of money. Instead we spent money on eating out for dinner.The location of the hotel was very good. It was a very close walk to Arc de Triomphe and the Charles de Gaulle Etoile Metro Station (Wagram exit). It was also a very short walk to the Air France shuttle stop on Ave Carnot, which took us to CDG Airport at the end of our stay. You can take this shuttle irrespective of what airline you are flying with.The streets in the area seem pretty safe, although it is important to use common sense. We did see some homeless people on Ave de Wagram, as well as youth hanging out into the night. Pickpockets are present in most tourist areas, so consider using a money belt and avoid taking out your wallet on streets and metro.Overall, we were quite pleased with this hotel for our vacation in Paris.Enjoy your trip.

<Author>rosstucker
<Content>honest value in Paris This is a very good hotel -- for Paris. A visitor to Paris must accept certain things for a three-star hotel such as this: the room will be small, the walls will be thin, and the guest will feel as if he is only one of many visitors moving through the hotel day by day. But this little hotel offers the extras one would want: a convenient location two streets up from the Arc de Triomphe, an ample breakfast, and -- most importantly -- a staff who seem to care for the wellbeing of the guest. The front desk is cheerful and helpful, and even the cleaning staff help with luggage and special requests. And -- there is air conditioning! The only real complaint one could have is -- and it's not the hotel's fault -- that the street -- a side street that is not all that busy --is noisy: there seem to be a lot of young undesirables hanging around the clubs and restaurants on the street. (However, the hotel's windows close tightly, and 80% of the noise is shut out.)

<Author>gtpatton
<Content>Pretty Good, We were Happy. Our family of four; with one 15 year old daughter and one 11 year old daughter stayed for two nights. Of course rooms were small [Paris, city typical]. We had suite #411, 4th floor which consisted of two rooms and bathroom. The first living room was small and when couch folded out to bed it took up whole room, and bathroom was directly off this room, so noise could be heard from bathroom to people sleeping here. Also, hotel has hard wired LAN connection in room and wireless in lobby. So I could not get up early to surf internet/ do work as small desk where LAN was located was on side of daughters bed. Had to go to lobby. Breakfast was 12 euros extra, but McDonalds 50 meters away... but McDonalds does not open until 7:30 AM which is really 7:45 AM as workers move slowly here. To sum up room, although not spacious, it was clean and modern. The bathroom was modern. This is what we really wanted and we got- clean and modern. Yes the elevator only fits one person, so use the stairs. The biggest bonus is location! We were very happy with location. When I booked, I thought I would have to take my family to Latin quarter to show off cafe's, patisseries, and French street character... but no, the neighborhoods around Magda are great. One block from Arc-de-Triumph and can catch Metro anywhere from here. But one block in the other direction are trendy streets with cafe's and shops. My 15 year old was in and out of all, looking for a certain type of gladiator sandal that she saw all the girls wearing.For two nights, avoiding the big brand name hotels, this boutique hotel was just fine. Again, clean and modernized which we think are most important.

<Author>ClareVancouver
<Content>Good Location The first thing we noticed was the great location of this hotel. As mentioned in the other reviews, only a couple of minutes from the Arc De Triumphe. It is also a very short walk to the Metro which, in my opinion, is the fastest and most convenient way to get around Paris. The hotel itself is very tastefully decorated. As previously mentioned by other reviewers, the lift is tiny and a bit claustrophobic so only one person at once with the cases. I don't usually like to mention size of rooms, but this room was particularly small. Literally, just little big bigger than the bed and not much room for our two cases. As we were on the fifth floor, we had also had a balcony. The room and bathroom were very tasteful and clean. We also found the staff on reception to be very friendly and helpful with any requests we had. The breakfast was good if you go down to the foyer level to eat (it is buffet style). On one of the mornings, we ordered breakfast to the room and got a very small amount for the 12 Euros (same price as buffet). I would highy recommend this hotel for couples going to Paris.

<Author>j32063
<Content>Small but good I spent a week at the Royal Magda from May 8th-14th and was satisfied with my experience. As other reviews here state, it is a clean, modern, well-run place with cheerful, helpful staff. The location is good, with the Air France shuttles and Metro right around the corner, as well as several cafes nearby. The hotel is a good choice as long as you understand that in Paris, price tends to be determined by size. Your first clue to the dimensions of your room should be the elevator, which is big enough for one person plus a suitcase OR 2 people. There were 2 of us in our room...a standard double with shower...and we had to do some serious organizing of our things in order to have floor space to walk. Everything in the room is fine; the bed was decent, the bathroom was tiny but modern and clean, and there was a flat-screen TV and even a mini-bar. However, for most Americans, the size of the room is about what you would expect from a walk-in closet, so if you are a large person you may be in for some severe claustrophobia.I would consider staying here again, although it might be more interesting to try something else within the price range. I have been able to afford better in the past, but frankly for about twice the price I only got about 25% more space and comfort.

<Author>cmelBelfast
<Content>Quaint and tidy Stayed here in the summer of 2007 with my girlfriend. Although, i'm mostly confirming what everyone else says in their reviews I thought i would add my comments.The location is excellent and although i'd read the reviews I was still pleasantly surprised at just how close it is to the L'Arc De Triomphe. It literally is 2 minutes walk, and thats if you take your time.The staff mostly stayed out of our way and although you could say they werent terribly helpful, when approached for advice or service they were actually very pleasant, and as with most parts of Paris, all I spoke to had very good English.Our room was nicely decorated and because it was on the top floor it was an odd shape with ceilings etc but still a nice size and very tidy. Take note that the location of the hotel means there are essentially no views of the city as its surrounded by buildings the same size.I give it a solid 4star review as its reasonable price and excellent location mean its brilliant for short stays like our city break.

<Author>emceeManchester
<Content>Sounds not too good...... As always I did my homework  read lots of reviews on TripAdvisor before I booked. To be fair I was not too disappointed. The location is great. The staff always polite  very helpful. The room clean  bathroom well appointed. However I was let down by two points. Firstly the air conditioning for the overall hotel was not switched on. The room was stuffy  a little uncomfortable at night. The manager was most apologetic  offered compensation. It was eventually working by the third ( last night). If this is an issue for you, before you book check with the hotel that the air conditioning is fully operational. The second point is more concerning. I was travelling with my two children (aged 14  8 years)  we were therefore in bed by 10.30pm. However most other residents were getting ready to go out at that time  were returning to the hotel between midnight  3am. I know because I could hear every last noise they made. The hotel does not appear to have considered sound insulation whilst refurbishing the property. Consequently you hear every door being slammed shut  double-locked, footsteps above you sound like a herd of elephants and- believe me- you can hear just about everything when an adjacent bathroom is being used....... I mean everything!!! Had I been travelling with a partner and staying up late then perhaps this would not have been so off-putting. But considering the biggest part of your stay in a hotel is sleeping, then perhaps this requires some attention by the management. If you're a heavy sleeper or such noises don't bother you then this truly is a fantastic base from which to explore Paris.

<Author>1stCEB
<Content>Great Hotel, but Beware the French ;-) My wife and I visited this hotel during a recent weekend. The previous reviews are accurate = good service  great location (to Metro, Air France Shuttle, Champ Elysees). We arrived early and had to leave our bags, while we explored the area. When we came back they had already placed our bags into our room (nice touch). The elavator is SUPER tiny, so get ready to make several trips. We would recommend a Suite, as the rooms are very tiny. With the Junior Suite we were able to fit our bags, no problem. Room was somewhat clean - some dirt near door, which was odd - but the bathroom was very clean. Our phone was a Pulse phone, versus a Tone, so had to use my cell phone for checking voice-mails, etc....Front desk receptionists were very helpful and polite. No need to rent a car, the Metro will get you everywhere, BUT beware of people trying to squeeze behind you when you pass through the Metro gates (turnstiles). My wife and I got a serious scare when a guy tried to force his way through, almost glued to my wife, with her ticket. He then cursed my wife and spit on the ground in front of us, when we confronted him! As if we were doing something wrong! Furthermore, beware the taxi drivers - they try to charge you 1 Euro per Suitcase - even though this isn't written anywhere. You really don't need a taxi with the Metro being so convenient. We REFUSED to use a taxi after this woman taxi driver tried to rip us off, stating that this is Paris and this is the way it is! I guess the taxi meters don't mean anything then. So, bottom-line, great hotel and location, but beware the locals as they try to take advantage of you. Keep your guard up please!

<Author>nadiasmyth
<Content>Fantastic hotel! We stayed in this hotel over the Easter week-end and let me just tell you what a fantastic time we had. We flew from Shannon to Paris Beauvais airport, shuttle bus dropped us at the Port Maillot, which is only 2 stops away by Metro from the hotel, but we decided to have a little walk and less than 10 min later we were in the welcoming lobby of the Royal Magda Etoile. Check in was so quick and efficient that in no time we were going up in the tiny elevator to our room on the 6th floor. As mentioned before 鈥?rooms are small but have everything you need, bed is extremely comfortable and bathroom is full size with a bathtub with a very good water pressure in the shower. Our room no 611 had a lot of windows which made our room feel very bright even on the dull, rainy day (yes, the weather was very bad all week-end). We didn鈥檛 have breakfast in the hotel, but it smelled lovely every morning in the lobby. Location of the hotel is fantastic; you are 2 min walk from the Arc de Triomph, Champs Elysee and metro station. You are only few minutes away from great selection of restaurant, bars, shops and etc. And this good location means a lot, especially if the weather is so bad and rain is just pouring non-stop, we could run to restaurants, metro and even La Duree (for some macaroons) without getting soaked wet :) Check out was as quick as check in and took less than 5 min, giving us time for a cup of coffee before our bus trip to Beauvais airport. Despite the bad weather we had an amazing week-end in Paris and we would like to thank all the fantasticl staff for making our stay so pleasant. For the price you pay for this hotel I would rate Royal Magda Etoile as a hidden gem of Paris.

<Author>STN74
<Content>Good value hotel - some street noise The hotel has a very pleasant staff.Breakfast 鈧?12 p.p is a little pricy and not very well stocked.Rooms aren't to small.All rooms have seen recent redecorating and the standard rooms do have the same decor as shown on the hotel website photos.There is relatively little traffic noise although the hotel is situated just a short stroll from the Wagram avenue and the Arch de Triomph.As there is a couple of bars and a night club in the right next to the hotel, you will experience some noise during the night, especially friday through monday nights.Plenty of restaurants in the neighboorhood.Short walk to metro stop: Charles de Gaulle EtoileThe Yellow metro line will take you directly to the city centre in minutes. The metro stop is also trafficated by the RER A-line witch connects to the RER B-line at Chatelet Les Halles, which takes you to either Charles de Gaulle or Orly airports. Fare: approx 鈧?16 p.p.Otherwise taxi takes about 20 minutes from Orly and costs approx. 鈧?0. Traffic depending.Rooms have no air-conditioning, and I suppose that you will most likely miss this during mid-summer.(Another tip: if you go to Paris during early spring be sure to bring warm clothing)

<Author>carugo
<Content>Lovely Hotel in a Great location! We have just returned from Paris after staying a long week-end at the Royal Magda with our 8 and 6 year old. We had a deluxe suite which is basically 2 rooms divided by an arch with a king size in one and a made up sofa bed in the other. Both rooms had a tv and the bathroom was lovely - sparkling clean - as was the rest of the hotel. We had good bathroom toiletries and the shower was excellent. The staff were very accommodating. We were very close to the Arc de Triomphe and the Champs Elysees. As other guests have stated, all transport was just at the end of the street too. All in all the location was great. We ate at Hippopotamus which was lovely and good for children, we also ate at Bistro Romain on Champs Elysees (top floor - good view of Champs at night). We had a one breakfast at Cafe de Flore on Boulevard Sain-Germain which was wonderful and worth the visit (one of the oldest cafes in Paris), and we had a lovely breakfast at the hotel one day. All in all a lovely trip!

<Author>zimozzie
<Content>Great location, great hotel My sister and I stayed at the Royal Magda Etoile for 2 nights on our way back from the UK to Australia. The staff were very friendly and especially helpful with advice about the buses and the metro.The foyer has the feel of a luxury, boutique hotel. The red tourist bus stops a short walk from the hotel (although this was great for getting around several landmarks, the sound system giving the commentary was poor and the bus was old).We would definitely stay at the Royal Magda Etoile when we go back to Paris.

<Author>loreleo
<Content>Oustanding Value in Paris The Royal Magda Etoile Hotel in Paris is one of the best deals in Paris. I have been at the Royal Magda Etoile twice during the last 6 months, and each time I received an outstanding treatment from the great staff. The rooms were always very clean, comfortable, and quiet. During the last visit (Febr 2008), I was upgraded to a large suite at no charge. The position of the Hotel is excellent, just in front of the Arc de Triomphe, minutes away from several Metro stations and the RER (train) station. In addition, the Hotel is minutes away from the Bus stop of the Air France shuttles that provide the fastest connection to both Airports in Paris (CGD and Orly). The only weakness of the Magda is probably the breakfast, but there are plenty of Cafes around to get fresh croissants. I strongly recommend the Royal Magda Etoile Hotel to business travelers (Paris Congress Center is only minutes away), to tourists and to everybody that want to enjoy Paris at an affordable price range.

<Author>JoolsDarlington
<Content>very friendly This hotel compares very favourably with others that we've stayed in in Paris. It was a little more expensive than our usual, but as my husband and I said, it was a treat to be in a room that was better than OK: Not a single bad-taste plastic-framed picture on the wall or a mildewed tile in the bathroom. Instead, everything was spick and span - lovely new tiles, pristine clean floor, piles of fluffy white towels, towelling dressing gown. We asked and were given extra pillows, and the chamber-maid greeted us with a smile every morning. The reception staff were unvariably charming and pleasant. We didn't eat breakfast in the hotel. As everyone else has said, the location was perfect. The area is totally unthreatening, even at night-time, with handy small shops nearby for water, bread and fruit. Our children (4 and 2) both love the Hippopotamus restaurant at Place des Ternes (5 mins on foot) and Bistro du 17ieme on Avenue de Villiers (15 mins on foot) was really great for an all inclusive Sunday lunch (I think it was about 36 Euros each including wine, aperitif and 3 courses - don't expect a children's menu, but waiters were very accommodating about half portions, children's portions etc). The Parc Monceau is handy for children to let off steam (hundreds of joggers at the weekend!) and the children's play area at Jardin de Luxembourg is brilliant, though you have to pay for access to it. The hotel was perfectly placed for so many activities.

<Author>Bariblak
<Content>Great Location Just returned from a 3 day trip to Paris with my wife and young daughters. I booked the Royal Magda after reading the reviews on this site, and we were not disappointed. We booked a Deluxe Suite, which is basically a bedroom and a lounge that contains a sofa bed. This was fine for us, but I would suggest the sofa is only big enough for 1 adult or 2 small children. The hotel was in excellent decorative condition and the staff we all exceptionally helpful and friendly. We had breakfast at the hotel because it was convenient but, at 12 euros a head, this was a mistake particularly as the kids were only having a croissant and hot chocolate. Better to turn left out of the hotel and find a patisserie or creperie. The breakfast area was very quiet each morning, so I suspect most people had elected to eat out.The location was excellent. Turn right out of the hotel, walk 20-30 metres, and you are looking at the Arc de Triomphe. Considering we were so central, the hotel was exceptionally quiet. Overall you will not be diappointed with this hotel. Keep an eye on the rates though, because they do offer substantially discounted rates occasionally . If you are unable to get a booking here, i noticed a number of similar hotels in the immediate areawhich are probably worth checking out.

<Author>Just&Rach
<Content>A Little Gem In A Perfect Location Myself, my wife, and our two good friends stayed here for two nights at the end of January. We booked the hotel via Hotels . com with help from Trip Advisor based on previous reviews.Most hotels are quite pricey in the centre of Paris, however this one is definitely value for money. Only a 15 euro, 15 minute, cab journey from the Gare Du Nord, it is also easily reachable from the nearest metro stop apprx 200 yards away. In advance of our stay, I emailed the hotel to check a few things, and like some of the other reviewers, found Yohan to be extremely helpful and very prompt in his replies. It is the little touches like this that make all the difference. The hotel, although quite small, was immaculate, and the rooms were spotless. All the staff were friendly and were always there to assist if needs be. The location was even better than we were led to believe, with the Arc De Triomphe on the doorstep along with all manner of shops, bars and restaurants. We also spent a day at Disney, and were very fortunate to also find that the metro stop by the hotel is a direct line to the park (about 40 minutes) but makes it extremely easy to get there and back if you are heading up that way. Paris is a great city to walk round, and the Eiffel Tower is around 35/40 minutes walk away, and the Louvre around 50 minutes straight down the Champs D'elysees.All in all, we can thoroughly recommended this hotel and would definitely stay there when we next venture into Paris. Although eating and drinking is often very expensive in the city, the Eurostar return trip via Ebbsfleet only cost 拢59 per couple with a promotion, so there is really no excuse not to explore this great place!

<Author>LifeboatJim
<Content>Fantastic Location!! Great Paris Hotel!! Just returned from 4 night stay at the Magda. Firstly the Air France shuttle which anyone can use stops within a 5 minute case drag of the hotel (20 Euros Return from T1 or T2 CDG). The Arc is only a 5 minute (if that) walk away as is a Metro station. The Louvre is within walking distance (30 - 45min), there are many good quality restaurants nearby as well as budget ones. MacDonalds is also at the end of the street if you fancy avoiding the 6 Euro coffees around Paris. Also at the end of the road is a self service restaurant (Monte Carlo), 2 courses for 11 Euros. Worth a go as food v good considering the cost. The night before paid over 100 Euros for 2. Found the staff very friendly and helpful at the hotel. Room was very clean and a good size for Paris. Breakfast was good, many people complain in reviews about the 12 Euro charge. I regularly pay 15GBP in the UK so found it good value for money. The street outside can get a little noisy at night but nothing clsoing the window doesn't sort. After all Paris is a cosmopolitan city so unlike many places people aren't in bed for 10pm. Recommend the Magda and Paris!!!

<Author>azuresky
<Content>So convenient! We stayed at the Magda Etoile over Christmas for 4 nights and I honestly don't think we could have made a better choice.For the pros; this place has got one of the BEST locations. Really easy to get to all the usual touristy sites (Eiffel tower, Louvre, Notre Dame, Sacre Coeur etc) by metro. The closest station is Charles de Gaulle which has about 3 lines running through it, and just around the corner is the Champs Elysees.Rooms were spotless, especially the bathroom which was great and linens were changed everyday. They even left us a box of divine Leonidas choccies on Christmas day! There are lots of wonderful brasseries close by and the staff are very helpful and knowledgeable about the area. We were a bit worried by some of the reviews regarding staff; but we encounted no such problems during our stay.As for the cons: The rooms and the bathroom are pretty tight (we stayed in a standard room) but perfectly adequate. Also, you can occassionally get the waft of smoke in your room as other patrons may be smokers but this generally dissapates quite quickly. There is no breakfast included in the room rate; but not really a problem as there are lots of great cafes nearby. Finally, this is not really a con but just something to note: there is supposed to be a 24hr reception, but we came home after midnight mass on Christmas Eve (around 2am) and found the door locked. We rang the doorbell, and it was answered straightaway so there was no problem but just something to be aware of if you are planning any late nights out.

<Author>Travelling_Deborah
<Content>Slightly disappointed I have just arrived home from Paris and my stay at the Royal Magda EtoileI booked this hotel based on the outstanding reviews on tripadvisor - especially in regard to service and location.The hotel was as expected - it is a 'boutique' hotel so you can't expect all amenities. Though I could imagine the room could be a bit cozy for two people.The rooms were very clean - but unfortunately no view except into the inner courtyard.The downside for me was - as for a recent reviewer - was the young man at the desk. Her colleagues at night were also lovely and friendly - one man from Morocco (who was on most of my stay) and the other from Algiers. They wre happy to chat and be helpful.The location of the hotel is fantastic but even at such reasonable prices I would hesitate to stay here again as your hotel is your home away from home and I don't like to feel like I am being a nuisance 'at home'.

<Author>peainpod
<Content>Good rather than great Like many others, we booked the hotel on the strength of the excellent reviews and rating from this site. While we weren't disappointed with our choice, in all honesty, I felt that the hotel didn't merit such a high ranking.Some of the good points mentioned in other reviews are certainly valid: great location (near CDG-Etoile station, 2 streets away from Air France drop-off) and good value for money (we paid $149 euros per night in early Dec). And our room was even somewhat larger than we had expected.That said, there were a number of less than satisfactory things as well. First off, our room had a lingering smoked-in smell that lasted for the first 2-3 days of our week-long stay. Hotel staff were inconsistent in service attitude and certainly not as friendly as one might expect in such an intimate setting. One dark-haired youth veered on rude in his attitude, even though we were just asking about the most mundane question (directions for this one restaurant) and the encounter was unpleasant enough that I studiously avoided him for the rest of the stay. My advice is to only ask reception questions when there was either a girl on duty (she was super friendly and that *almost* but not quite made up for the insolent rude young guy) and a middle-aged gentlemen.On the whole, we were still not disappointed with our choice and would even probably choose it again - but just thought that a more balanced review would help to warn future guests from having too high expectations and becoming disappointed.

<Author>NYorkers
<Content>mixed feelings We stayed at the Magda Etoile for three nights this November. We booked it after reading the glowing reviews on Tripadvisor, thinking it would be an impeccable experience. The many 5.0 ratings are convincing, yet a bit misleading.First off, the location is truly terrific. Having been to Paris many times, I can attest to the fact that the Magda Etoile is in a great location to see the city. It is around the corner form the 1 line, which crosses Paris horizontally and takes you pretty much everywhere. The stop is called Charles de Gaulle-Etoile. From the hotel it's about a minute on foot.Now for the buts...The hotel is small, one could say intimate, and rooms are not very large. They are very very clean, but our room had clearly been smoked in. The smoke smell was quite intense and if you're very sensitive, you'd be mad, I guarantee it. The bath towels we used after showering, upon arrival, smelled strongly of smoke. I called reception and we received new ones, but I will admit that it skeeved us out that we had the previous guests bath towels on the shelf... he/she didn't use them, but still...Then, the front desk. The girls were great, helpful and pleasant. But one scraggly, skinny dude we asked to make a reservation for us couldn't have been more arrogant. When we asked him to call a well-known restaurant to see if we could get a table, he insisted it was a chain and that there was another one nearby, which we should just walk to. I knew for a fact that wasn't the case, so when I asked him to find the one I meant in St. Germain, he asked if I had the telephone number...like as in call them yourself. I said i could look it up online, but that I was hoping he could make the call, since my French is rudimentary and sometimes it helps when a hotel calls. He sighed...he made me wait...then he said he would call back...and didn't. When my husband went downstairs and asked him, he seemed put out and said he hadn't had time yet to find the number, along with the roll of the eye. In short, he was a jerk. It kind of colored our view of the rest of the staff, perhaps unfairly.The breakfast was ok, but at 12 euros per person not exactly good. Some croissants, some baguette, wrapped cheese, jam...coffee..oh well.So all in all it's not a total disappointment, it's an adequate hotel, but we won't give it a 5.0. We decided not to drink the Kool-Aid..;-)  
<Date>Nov 30, 2007

<Author>EuroReisen
<Content>Wonderful Spent two nights at the Royal Magda and had a wonderful time. The hotel is well-situated just off the CDG Etoile and is very near the Metro stop of the same name and also the AIr France airport bus stop.I arrived early in the afternoon and was able to check in right away, and from the very beginning the staff were warm, friendly and welcoming. My single room included a double bed, bathroom with shower, LCD TV, free broadband internet, and a desk. Everything was spotlessly clean and the bathroom had huge, fluffy towels.Breakfast was not included in the room price and was offered as either a buffet in the lobby or a tray delivered to the room. As the charge was the same for either option (12 Euros), I had a tray in my room and it was the perfect way to start my day: cafe au lait, fresh squeezed orange juice, yogurt, baguette, croissant, pain au chocolat, cheese, butter, and jam. I decided to order breakfast at the last minute and it was brought up less than 10 minutes after I called. It's also available until noon should you want to really sleep in.The only thing less than perfect was the soundproofing of the room. I could hear every word spoken by the couple in the next room, and whenever they would leave or return, it sounded like they were opening and closing my door. And, although perfectly adequate, an upgrade in the bedding wouldn't be a bad idea.For the location, price and service quality, though, the Royal Magda is a gem. I can't wait to return.  
<Date>Nov 25, 2007

<Author>rosenbear
<Content>Lovely We stayed for five nights at the Magda and had a great stay.The location was perfect - right near the Arc de Triomphe and the train station, so we could get everywhere we needed to go easily.There were plenty of eateries nearby, plus the staff were happy to point us in the direction of an internet cafe and supermarket.The room and bathroom were pretty tiny, but very well furnished and clean.We found the daily cleaning always seemed to be fairly late in the day, so coming back for an afternoon siesta was out of the question, but there's so much to do in Paris that wasn't a huge issue!We checked out fairly early one morning, and the man at the desk was more than happy to book us a taxi and help us carry out our luggage when it arrived.The Magda has a great, friendly atmosphere - highly recommended. <Author>CBFOUR
<Content>Excellent disabled room We booked the disabled room, which is located besides the reception and we stayed five nights in the hotel. The room had enough space for the two wheelchairs of my wife (one for normal use and one to be connected to a electric powered wheel). While I was having business meetings she could go where she wanted go through entire Paris autonomously, because most sidewalks are lowered down to street level at the corners. The room was very clean and very quiet! Especially the latter is rare in noisy Paris! There are some good restaurants in the vicinity. The entrance of the hotel is also rather good for wheelchairs. From the sidewalk only a little step of 2 - 4 cm has to be taken. Most wheel chair drivers can manage that. When ever you have a problem, the people at the reception are very friendly and helpful. In my view this room is very adequeate for people in a wheelchair. Some positive suggestions for the management: 1. In the bathroom there is no screen or curtain to prevent water splashing on the ground surface. It was no problem for my disabled wife when she took a bath, but when I took a shower, standing upright, I could not prevent that a lot of water came on the ground surface. 2. Also the flexible water supply is too short for a normal person taking a shower. Holding the shower head just above my head it sqeezed off the water supply. 3. Further, the place to put your bath room stuff (shaving kit, make up and other things) is far to small. Twice, I moved my hair comb on the one side and at the other side of the glass plank the glass fell into the sink. It was broken both times (sorry manager...). Anyhow, the next time that we will come to Paris, we will again go to this hotel.

<Author>EricToronto
<Content>Perfect for Paris My fiancee and I stayed at the Royal Magda for a week as part of our honeymoon. Paris is beautiful and the Royal Magda is a wonderful hotel to stay in to see the city. A short walk from the Metro, the hotel is ideal for tourists. Across from the Metro is the Arc and a 30 second walk from there is the Champs d'Elysse. We stayed on the 6th floor with a view of the other rooms. Not much to look at. The television is tiny (13inches at best) and the fridge was fully stocked making it difficult to keep any food in. The lift is not for the larger individual. Two people, max. and don't expect to fit any luggage in the lift with you. Showers are decent size by European standards. The Royal Magda receives such a high rating because for what you pay, you get a decent value. The beds are nice but small. The a/c works well. The front desk people are nice (although Yohan broke the handle on our luggage by accident) - the hotel has offered to reimburse us. The location is excellent. We truly enjoyed our stay here. I don't know what the other rooms are like but for a honeymoon couple, I would highly recommend staying here. On a side note, try the Chinese restaurant across from the hotel. We ate here twice and were very happy with our meals and the price. There's a McDonald's on the corner and the neighbourhood is pleasant to walk during the day. There are few nice, small cafe's and eateries on McMahon.

<Author>Marigot1
<Content>What a great fiind We stayed at the Magda Etoile for 2 nights last week on our way home from Provence. This was our 6th trip to Paris, and we have stayed in many different hotels. The Magda Etoile was an excellent bargain for the location and accomodations. We had a 2 room suite- with a queen size bed. Our room faced the rear of the building, (not streetside) and was very quiet. The bed and pillows were quite comfortable. What made this hotel special was the location (right near the Arc D'Triumphe and Metro stop) and the kindness of the front desk staff. We had emailed the hotel prior to our arrival with some restaurants that we wanted to book . They went over and above to secure reservations, even when one of the restaurants was completely booked. They were also ready to give detailed directions to a restaurant or information as to which terminal we need for check in at Charles De Gaulle . FInally, one of the front desk staff assisted us in taking our bags to the nearby Airfrance bus to go back to the airport.  We booked through the website and while there were made aware that there were some far less expensive rooms-- albeit smaller and facing the street (with attendant noice from the bar next door). In all, this hotel was a great find, and we would not hesitate to return.

<Content>Great little hotel This hotel was booked by my husband as part of a surprise first anniversary trip to Paris.The best thing about the hotel is it's location. A stone's throw away from the Arc de Triomphe and Champs Elysees, and one of the main metro stations: Charles de Gaulle Etoile.It's on a quiet street, except on Saturday nights when the club next door plays music well into the night, but to be honest, once the door to the balcony is closed, it's not really audible.We had a club room on the 5th floor, and whilst it was small, it was perfectly formed with a spotlessly clean bathroom. <Author>LovedParis
<Content>Very French, Very Nice Great hotel. Our first trip to France, and they were very accomodating. We arrived at about 9:00 AM, I had asked for an early check in and they were very accomodating, had us checked in within 5 minutes. Very helpful with directions, and in securing a reasonably priced shuttle back to the airport. (Much cheaper 34euros, than what I booked to come to the hotel over the internet.) Hotel was very clean, bathroom was small, but we expected that. We stayed in room 214, usually took the stairs, unless our excursions had us totally exhausted. Elevator was broken (as they said, Out of Work) for one day, but no big deal. Great location, nice lobby to sit and read the paper and have a glass of wine - which was reasonable at 5 euros. Only thing that I would have wished was for better internet access, I used the access to the Club Etoile across the street (great connection from the lobby), but would have paid more to get wireless access.

<Author>PENNYTHEBEAST
<Content>Bravo Hotel Magda! I had confidence about this hotel from the reviews. There are many boutique hotels in the same area, most of them three star, all look inviting and lovely. However, I can only tell you about Royal Magda as that's where we slept for four nights.Traveling with two children we had a room/studio with a sofa bed for the kiddies and a queen bed for us. The rooms could however be completely closed off, if privacy was needed. The studio was lovely, very, very clean, inviting, perfect. Studio had mini bar, both rooms had TV's.........however, apart from CNN and BBC news, all the channels were French, no option to order movies.Where the Magda excelled (and we've stayed in some of the very best hotels in the world) was the concierge and service. Firstly, breakfast continued till noon, and without any extra cost you can have it served in your room. Its a continental breakfast, pastries, cold meats, cheeses, juices and hot drinks, very fresh, very yummy.Location, location, location, five mins to Champs Elysee and the Arch de Triomph. two mins to a McDonalds.........and the very delicious McFlurries (sorry). Across the street, there was a very unassuming Chinese restaurant. After eating lunch at The Jules Verne (Eiffel Tower) we popped in here for an easy dinner, it was in fact one of our best meals we had in all our travels (ouch!), a very good Chinese.The ladies and gentlemen at reception, all very helpful and professional. All very sweet to our girls. A calming influence on the whole hotel.The most amazing thing that I was delighted with, after being to Paris a handful of times prior. The Magda was quiet at night. Silent. One night some teenagers left there window open and were chatting......the noise did travel, but they were soon told to close their window and make good use of the A/C.I rated this hotel with the full five stars, because I found absolutely no fault in it. I thought it was a steal at the cost, a terrific find (thanks to Trip advisor), a perfect solution to enjoying Paris to it fullest! Bravo Hotel Magda.

<Author>LanceScotland
<Content>Romantic, very pleasant stay We've just returned today (30th July) from a 4 night break. We loved this hotel. Booked it up from trip advisor reviews and were pleased with the results. We had a club room on front of street, Paris rooms and lifts to floors are compact so do not expect lots of space, for us it was perfect. Very close by to Air France bus which we used from CDG airport which took around 45 mins. Lots of bistros, etc all around and easy walking distance to metros. Staff very helpful - just tell them what you're looking for and they'll help (even before your stay by e-mail)! We asked for a room on the front and yes it can be a bit noiser at weekends but soundproofing is good and actually we loved it, we felt very much part of it! Well worth a visit to this modern and perfectly formed small hotel. PS: breakfast is not included and is 12 euros per person - we actually just got breakfast out at local bakeries which cost us half the price, also bistros are cheaper to eat in than restaurants and try the specials of the day!

<Content>Very Disappointing! Have just returned from spending 3 nights at Royal Magda ,I cannot help wondering if I stayed in the same hotel as some of the other reviewers! The cleaning staff and breakfast staff were very friendly and polite and the gentleman on the reception desk at night was very helpful and obliging.The first problem arose when I asked Flore if she could suggest a restauramnt in the Pont Neuf area as we were gong on the Seine Cruise that evening and it departed from that area. I was amazed when her answer was no she did not know any restaurants in that area! Normally we would check out the net for restaurants but because I was led to believe that she was so helpful to other guests I decided to ask her. We eventually found our own restautant on the net!When we returned that evening I asked Flore if I could take a jug of iced water up to our room. She replied by asking me if I knew there was water in the minibar. Yes I did know but it was a jug of fresh water that I wanted and not bottled water as we had been drinking fresh water in the restaurants since we arrive. She returned with a litre bottle of water and said she would put it on our bill! She kept to her word and we were charged 3Euro on check out!The following evening I asked the night porter for the same jug of iced water and he duly obliged without hesitation!We are not loud or demanding customers and therefore I could not understand the indifference which we experienced. I have never felt so unwelcome in a hotel before and unfortunately although Paris was wonderful this experience has somewhat spoilt the memory.I was very angry when I returned home to discover my daughters were equally upset at our experience as they had arranged the trip for us to celebrate our wedding anniversary and had emailed the hotel to tell them this and to ask them if they could ensure that the trip was a good one. If you are taking a Seine Cruise the Vedettes du Pont Neuf are excellent and very good value. Two really good restaurants are Chez Clement (a chain of about 12 restaurants in various areas in Paris. We went twice to the one on the Champs Elysses and found excellend value and great food and if using the open top bus the Bus Rouge is great but the Open Bus (yellow one) is a bit dearer but stops in more places of interest to let passengers off.

<Author>AnPAncaster
<Content>Great little hotel Great little hotel. Spotlessly clean; can't emphasize that enough. Good internet, which meant that we could keep in touch with our kids at camp in Canada... <Author>sgd73
<Content>Charming little hotel! The Royal Magda is a charming little hotel just a few hundred metres from the Arc D'Triomphe and very close to the Charles De Gaulle Etoile Metro (and RER) station. Whilst the rooms (on the 3rd floor) are small, they are clean and nicely appointed, with modern bathrooms. The front desk staff are excellent; very friendly and helpful and the breakfast (continental) is quite good. Bear in mind if you have large suitcases that the lift is absolutely tiny, so a few trips might be necessary to get more than one person to the room:) In terms of close amenities, there is a little supermarket around the corner where you can buy cheap bottled water etc.. whilst the Restaurant (En Flamme) on Rue Wagram (across the street at the end of Rue Troyon) is exceptional! (Try the Roast Chicken or, for a real treat, the Steak Tartare). Whilst it's a fairly long (but enjoyable) walk along the Champ Elysees to other landmarks (The Louvre, The Seine, various Bridges, Notre Dame, Le Conciergerie etc..) the close Metro and RER station make travelling a breeze. We found that catching the train to Chatalet Metro station was the most convenient stop close to major landmarks. Overall, can definitely recommend the Royal Magda as a charming, boutique hotel which is easily accessible by foot or train to a lot that Paris has to offer!

<Author>RBB-7
<Content>Incredibly Honest treatment I was just reading the July 2007 issue of consumer reports. The Hotel reviews had a special section on High Fees- Guest gouging is on the rise article on page 13.  Also -Bottom Line magazine just had a top 10 list of ways that hotels add on extra charges.Here is my experience with the concierge (Yohan) at the Royal Magda Etoile in Paris. My wife an I were stuck in London and could not get on the Chunnel train because of a railyard fire in southern England. We were supposed to check in at the royal Magda and couldn't for obvious reasons. Orbitz was the booking agent and was impossible to reach by phone. I held on for 20 minutes (at $1.50 per) and was cut off. Second try - here is the Orbitz recorded message - (paraphrased)Don't call us anymore . There is bad weather on the East coast and we don't want to talk to you until tomorrow.I tried to have my concierge in London cancel the reservation in Paris by internet. He told me that he had. He hadn't , and even if he had ,the way that the Orbitz booking was worded - they would get all three days that we paid for anyway- around $640 whether we showed up in Paris or not.Here's where the story gets good. I called Yohan and said that we couldn't make the connection. He said (in perfect English) if you can get here tomorrow we'll take care of you (actually there were about 6 phone calls). Next day the Eurostar took us to Paris and Yohan true to his word gave us a room for 2 days at a terrific rate which we paid for. He also said that he had not received word that the Orbitz cancellation was official and that they might still be paid for our booking under the original contract. If they got paid by Orbitz they would refund our money (around $420). HUH? YEAH RIGHT!Well guess what? In May I get a call from Paris. It's Yohan. Mr. Bradshaw we have received payment from Orbitz - may I have your Card information so that we can issue you a refund?I received a full Mastercard credit two days later. My wifeand I are very grateful to Yohan in particular. We received spectacular treatment from him, but everyone was very nice at the hotel.. Not all Hotels are out to gouge you -The Royal Magda Etoile sure isn't. Their management is as honest as the day is long. We had a great stay but it was too short. Next time it will be for a week. It's a great location. We'll be back next March for sure. If you can get a room, do it on their website, or call Yohan direct. Don't waste your time with Orbitz but do stay at the Royal Magda Etoile. It's a gem!  
<Date>Jun 19, 2007

<Author>pukamin
<Content>"Excellent hotel and great value" We just returned from a two night stay at the Royal Magda hotel and we found it to be one of the best, if not the best, of the hotels I had booked similar in size and class for our European vacation. The location was perfect, close to the the Arc de Triomphe and the Champs Elysees, as well as many restaurants, a boulangerie, and the metro. Our experience differed greatly from those of some other recent travellers. We arrived early and I had planned to check our luggage, but we were able to get into our room after a few minute wait. I had booked a junior suite for our family of four, which was sufficiently roomy and had a separate room with a pull-out sofa. The rooms were light and airy, with plenty of windows, air-conditioning, mini-fridge, and two televisions with CNN and BBC, both not available at any other hotel we had stayed in. The bathroom was large and beautiful. Everything was immaculately clean, and we were impressed by how quickly our rooms were cleaned, the beds made up, and our scattered belongings organized. My daughter had washed her skirt the night before and put it over a chair to dry, and we found it neatly hung up on the clothesline over the tub.The desk personnel patiently and politely answered my numerous questions, and made reservations for us at suggested (very nice) restaurants. The hotel elevator was not large enough for the four of us, but none of the elevators at the other five hotels we stayed at were either, so I did not find that to be a problem. We did not try the hotel breakfast because we did not want to pay extra, but there were plenty of places close by to get coffee and pastries, as well as a small grocery store not too far away for cheese and yogurt.The only minor complaint that I would have is that the bathtub has the the type of half shower divider wall that European bathrooms often have, which caused a few minor floods in the bathroom. Fortunately there were plenty of fluffy towels to soak up the puddles.The Royal Magda was the perfect hotel to end our vacation with. We will definitely be back.  
<Date>Jun 18, 2007

<Author>SueJenkins
<Content>Excellent Location, Average Hotel My husband and I booked this hotel for 4 nights for my birthday after reading the wonderful reviews and were somewhat disappointed with the Royal Magda. Having stayed there, it is a good value hotel, which was clean and in an excellent location.The rooms were very small and the bathroom tiny . We were on the fourth floor and could hear the family in the next rooms. There were only 3 pillows so had to take turns for the third pillow, the area to store all your clothes was extremely small and the space between the bed and the furniture and walls was so limited that it was difficult for the two of us to pass each other and we are not particularly big!Location: excellent. A short distance from the from the Champs Elysees and the Arc de Triomphe. This was the best feature of the hotel, in our opinion.Customer Service: Johan was very friendly and helpful although when I booked the hotel - their website stated that there was a late checkout facility, when we asked we were informed that we had to be out of our room by 12.30 at the latest. I asked the night clerk if there was somewhere we could wash and change before leaving for the airport and we were told 'no', although when we asked Johan again when checking out he did say we could use the toilets on the ground floor.Extras: We did not try the 12 euro/day breakfast, as there were very good brasseries in the local area. The lift was small, and only really held one person and a suitcase or two adults. I'd recommend the Royal Magda for budget travellers looking for a clean hotel for a good price. I just can't give this hotel the rave reviews that everyone else has. It wasn't one of the best hotel experiences we've had.Just a recommendation for other travellers staying here - try the Bistro Du 17 restaurant which is probably about 10 minutes walk away at 108 avenue de villiers. A excellent three course meal with a bottle of wine between two people is 34 euros per per person and is excellent.

<Author>Kona05
<Content>Another Positive Review We stayed at Royal Madga Etoile for three night from 5/27. We arrived around 9am, but the room was not ready as expected, so they offered to keep the luggage while we enjoy the sightseeing in Paris. After returning in the afternoon, they upgraded us to the Jr. Suite from the Club room, which was spacious and delightful. We didn't eat breakfast in the hotel, however, we enjoyed having their coffee in the morning for 3.5euros when we get up in the early morning (jetlag) as we realized most local restaurants are closed until 8~9am. Their coffee is more American style with generous portion as compared to all other hotels/restaurants we've visited during our entire trip. The coffee that we had in our room was served in a tray with a cup and a single-serving pot that was nice and hot.One day, we left our room around 8am for breakfast across the street and returned a little before 9am. As we walk toward our room, we noticed our door was open for room cleaning. Since we needed to get ready for our plan for the day, we were going to ask her to leave the room as is, but she said the room is already cleaned and she was just getting ready to leave.As we went inside the room, I could not believe how efficiently she had cleaned and organized the room! I mean, when we left, our room was a complete mess - shoes, socks, shirts, books, coins, sunglasses, candy wraps all over the place - as we were going to clean up ourselves after coming back from our breakfast. She managed to fold our clothes, stack books, arrange shoes, neatly put sunglasses and coins on the table, etc. As embarassing as it was, she did an amazing job and we were extremely impressed. In-room refrigerator was very convenient. We put some cheese and wine that we had bought from the nearby supermarket. The available English TV channels were CNN International and BBC World, but six other hotels we stayed during our France trip had only CNN if any, and it really didn't matter to us anyway because after a long day of exploring, we were dead tired and went to bed early right after coming back from dinner. Overall, we enjoyed staying at Royal Magda Etoile and definitely recommend this place for anyone looking for affordable, friendly , English-fluent hotel with convenient Metro access .

<Author>Eihtball99
<Content>Good Value, Great Location, Average Hotel Overall We were somewhat disappointed with the Royal Magda.I have to be honest...when I read all of the wonderful reviews, I thought this would be one of the best hotels in Europe. Having stayed there, it is a great value, but nothing to write home about. I'm still scratching my head that the Royal Magda won a Traveler's Choice award.Rooms: We switched rooms midway through the stay, to get a higher, quieter room. The street noise from the first floor is definitely noticeable, and the hotel is very old - you will know exactly when the folks above you are up and about.The rooms were small, as we expected, and there was a very heavy smell of smoke. (Not a big surprise in Paris) The bathroom was very clean, yet the shower had a door that only extended 1/2 way, so the bathroom kept getting soaked. Not a big deal, just not expected in such a highly rated hotel.Location: Fantastic. Two blocks from the Charles de Gaulle Etoile station, on the metro. A stone's throw from the Champs Elysees and the Arc de Triomphe. This was the best feature of the hotel, in our opinion.Customer Service: Johan and Flor were very friendly and accommodating. The night desk clerk was somewhat pushy and unfriendly. We wanted directions to a laundrette, and all he'd tell us was how to use their (expensive) cleaning service.Extras: We opted out of the 12 euro/day breakfast, as there were way to many brasseries in the local area. The lift was small, but worked great when lugging us up to the fifth floor. Oh, and the TV carried two English stations: BBC and CNN. It would've been great to have a non-news English station, for winding down at bedtime.Finally, I noticed in many of the other reviews for the Royal Magda, the reviewers had been given a free upgrade to a Junior Suite. I'm almost curious if this didn't skew the reviews, slightly. We weren't upgraded, so maybe our experience was a bit different than others.I'd recommend the Royal Magda for budget travelers looking for a clean hotel for a good price. I just can't give this hotel the rave reviews that everyone else has. It wasn't one of the best hotel experiences we've had.

<Author>travelduck111
<Content>A Class Act We recently had a one night fantastic stay at this classy hotel. Our journey began in Atlanta with a flight to Paris through Boston. We arrived in Paris after a cramped Air France flight where I wore the seat in front of me in my lap for six hours. Exhausted, we arrived at the hotel at 8:00 a.m. and was advised (not surprisingly) that our junior suite was not ready. I asked if we could leave our bags at the desk while we wait for the room. To our delight, Flore upgraded us to a suite and checked us in immediately. We went to sleep until noon and then had a full restful day in Paris. Without this gesture, we would have been tired throughout the day. A class act from this hotel. The hotel is absolutely spotless - not a crumb any place we looked. The furnishings are nice and comfortable. The bathroom and shower were great and I only made a tiny mess. The location is a quick walk from the AirFrance Bus stop and a stone's throw from the Arc de Triumphe. The hotel arranged dinner reservations for us at Cafe de L'Homme with a great view of the Eiffel tower at dusk. Outside the restaurant is the absolute best view of the Eiffel Tower. How about some Travelduck (Le Travelduck) tips for you?1. Take the AirFrance Bus from CDG to the Arc de Triumphe stop. I suggest you 'Google Earth' the hotel location. You will see the AirFrance buses and know your exact route to the hotel from the bus. Follow that tip and you will not get lost. If you are flying Delta from Atlanta or Boston, the bus stop at CDG is right outside baggage claim. Cost is 20 euro rt per person. 2. Cafe de L'Homme was great but not all tables have an Eiffel Tower view. It was raining so we could not sit outside and there are only about 2-3 tables right near the window. I guess my wife and I were not chic enough to get one of those tables but it was still a great dinner.3. Take the boat rides down the Seine River - save some walking and enjoy the ride.4. Get to the Eiffel Tower very early (like 8:30 a.m.) if you want to go to the top. Lines are very long!5. Enjoy a nice crepe during your stay in Paris. Be careful because the crepes are very hot when handed to you. The rude guy making my crepe (he told me to zip it after I repeated my order) shoved the crepe in my hand and made me spill my coffee. I left it there (bad duck).6. If you have a five hour layover in chilly Boston (like us), do not drag your wife all over the city searching for a crabcake sandwich. It will make a rough start to your trip - lucky we were going to Paris which ended the bad mood quick!Have a great stay at the Royal Magda and in Paris. I highly recommend it. Contact me for any further advise!

<Author>emmaAustralia
<Content>Perfect Position In Paris My husband and I stayed at the Royal Magda for 8 days in May and booked this hotel based on the mountains of positive reviews on this site. We were very pleased that we listened to our wise 'travel-advisors' because the hotel exceeded our expectations. Firstly, it is in a wonderful spot - very close to the metro and you could throw a 'euro' and hit 'The Arc'. Of course it is very, very, very touristy....but then we were tourists after all..although sometimes I had difficulty finding a french person amongst the throngs of Americans and Japanese...could be a turn-off to some.The staff were lovely - so helpful, the rooms were lovely and well-appointed(and not a bad size - I've had smaller in New York). The breakfast was also worth it - for us anyway. Yes 12 euro sounds alot (we had to convert to Australian dollars - so it is a PAINFUL process) but it was worth every cent...my husband putaway 3 coffees, cereal and 4-5 pastries every morning which would have set us back alot more than 12 euros on the street. The breakie is on until midday (and they don't seem to mind if you slip back later in the morning for another cup of coffee) and they will deliver it to your room if so desired.My only criticism (and it is a bit sad) is that the only english speaking channel was CBS (or some other American cable news program) - they had 2 great movie channels.. dubbed into French. Just one movie channel - even with subtitles would've been nice. Although France did elect a new President whilst we were there and due to the limited TV options we came home experts in French politics!!!Overall a great little boutique hotel that I would and already have recommended (to my parents for there next trip to Europe.) HOpe this is helpful!!

<Author>Angelpink
<Content>Lovely hotel, perfect location! Stayed here from 1st - 4th May for a girly getaway with my Mum and this was the perfect hotel. Hotel was so easy to find being just 2 streets away from the Air France pick up/drop off stop. We checked in at 10am without a problem. The room was spotless, yes as previously stated the rooms are very small but for the amount of time you spend in them they are perfect. The room had a mini bar which we emptied out onto the dresser and removed the shelves so we could keep water and more importantly wine in and the staff never had a problem with this as itwas all put back as it was before we checked out! The water pressure in the shower is superb, it really blasts the cobwebs away. The staffare brilliant, they speak excellent english and couldn't be more helpful. Location wise you couldn't ask for much better 2 min walk from the Metro, the Arc de Triomphe, Champs Elysees and the Le Cars Rouge stop if you want an open top bus tour!The only negative point I would comment on is the fact that mirrors are positioned so far away from the wall sockets, so it's quite awkward if your using straightners/curling irons, we solved the problem by putting the mirror on the chair.One tip I would give is to do the Arc de Triomphe at night as the night views of the city are spectacular and in my opinion better thanthe Eiffel tower!!I wouldn't hesitate in recommending this hotel and if I return to paris will definately stay here again!

<Author>CaptCanuck
<Content>Overall a very good experience. My wife and I stayed at the Magda Etoile for 3 nights in April of 2007.The staff is friendly and responsive, and the room we had - and the hotel in general - is nicely decorated.We were upgraded to a junior suite upon arrival, which was a nice surprise. The room was still a bit on the small size, but then I looked at the floorplan for the entire floor, and realized that we'd really lucked out. The standard rooms are very, very small. If you can afford it, go for a junior suite at minimum.As well, the location of the hotel is excellent - only 1.5 blocks away from a key metro station. It also doesn't hurt that when you emerge from the metro station the first thing you see is the Arc du Triomphe! Very nice.One complaint that I have is that one of the staff talked us out of going to the Moulin Rouge in favour of the Lido. The Lido show was absolutely terrible - I've subsequently heard that the Moulin Rouge is much better - and we couldn't help but wonder if the recommendation was based on pocketing a larger referral fee from Lido when she booked our tickets. It was a fairly big issue to us, because the Lido show cost us 200 Euros, for an embarrasingly amaturish and tedious evening. We expected better advice from the hotel staff.All that said, that unfortunate incident does not stop us from giving the hotel 5/5. Just do yourself a favour and do your own trip research on Paris before going, because you won't be able to count on unbiased advice in a tourist oriented city like Paris.
